< review>
I usually really dislike going to AT&T stores. I always leave feeling really disappointed and not getting what I wanted. To make a long story short, the Apple store told me I had to buy the iPhone X at the AT&T store because of my upgrade program. It was pretty bogus- they wouldn't let me pay them out of my current iPhone plan to get a new one even though my phone was completely dead. I was 10 days away from my 30 month plan being up. I went to AT&T and was immediately helped by Alberto. I told him my situation and he really listened AND he knew the exact issue I was talking about. He was so incredibly helpful and didn't just tell me to wait until the period was up in 10 days (like they did at 2 other AT&T stores earlier this year). He gave me options, he was going to call AT&T management and urge them to waive the block on my account so I could pay out of my plan that day. He said if that didn't work he would give me a phone to borrow for those 10 days. He was able to get the block waived and I was/am so relieved. He is so knowledgable and I would really recommend seeing him for any phone issues. He is not just another person working at AT&T and telling you no without having a solution. He was so much more helpful than any AT&T employee I have ever interacted with, and it's because he really understood my issue and also found it to be ridiculous that I could not get an upgrade so he figured it out for me. Alberto is the best!< /review>

< Text>
Update: After what happened, Jenny, the office manager called and was genuinely apologetic and helpful. She offered to comp us for what we spent at the vet as well as what we paid Animal Poison Control. She made it clear that she was very unhappy about what had happened and let us know that she had already spoken to all the staff and was planning to speak with Dr. Y herself when she returned to the office next week. The fact that she cared so much about their patients definitely earned them back a few points.
________________________
I took my dogs to this vet yesterday. I took them both in bc they were due on at least one of their shots and wanted to get one of their ears checked. The staff at the front were very patient while I looked through my dogs paperwork to figure out which shots they needed, which was nice.

I wasn't seen by Dr. Y bc she was out of the office, but by another vet. He was very kind and thorough. He told me that one of my dogs had tapeworms (which was not what I went in for, I felt like a terrible dog parent bc I never thought my dogs would get tapeworms)! I was thankful that he was so thorough and glad that I took my dogs in for a checkup. He recommended a different topical flea med to the one I had been using and gave both my dogs a prescription dewormer (Virbantel), and we were on our way home.

At this point, I was very happy with my experience. I gave both my dogs the meds as instructed and went about my evening. Before I went to bed I decided to look online for any possible side effects, just so I knew what to look for.

While I was looking this up I noticed the dosage recommendations. According to the manufacturer website, my one larger dog was given twice the recommended dose. At this point I started to get worried so I decided to look on some other websites for information. All of them recommended the same dose which was half the amount I had given my dog.

I called Dr. Y's, but they were closed, so I called the emergency number they recommend on their answering machine. The woman I spoke to from the Veterinary Specialty and Emergency Center was so helpful. I explained my predicament to her, she took my info down and called me back within 5 mins. She wasn't familiar enough with the med and recommended that I call Animal Poison Control.

I tried calling one more emergency animal clinic who were also so patient and helpful on the phone. I explained what happened, and they said that the amount I gave my dog was indeed twice the recommended dose. They told me that while the active ingredients in the Virbantel were not very dangerous, it would not be a bad idea to call Animal Poison Control and get their opinion.

It's 11pm at this point.  I called Animal Poison Control. They charge $49 for their consultation, which I paid. They said that the amount prescribed was an overdose, but that the med has a wide margin of safety, so my dog would be fine and to call my vet in the morning. It was a relief to know that this error wasn't going to hurt my dog.

I called Dr. Y's in the morning to check that they meant to give the dose. The woman I spoke to over the phone checked the computer as well as the post-it note that the vet had given her and said that the dosage was correct. I asked her to double check with the vet and call me back when he got in.

When she called back she said that I was right, that the vet had misread the label and that the next time I give my dog the med in two weeks, she only needs to take one. This is when I got even more upset. If I had my own veterinary establishment and INCORRECTLY prescribed the DOSE of a med, I would have been VERY apologetic, comped the visit, something. They said if I bring back the extra pill, that they would pay me the difference. When I said that I'm so glad that it wasn't a more toxic med and asked if this is something that happens, the woman over the phone said that they are human, and they do make errors... Yes, this is true, but you work in medicine, and any errors you make can be fatal, so you shouldn't be so nonchalant about it.</Text>

Already have spent a lot of money, gave J & J THREE chances to redeem themselves, but J & J has miserably failed to offer the appropriate muscular acupressure relief I sought to get there in the first place.
1st visit:(the most expensive session)
The masseur spent 15 to 20 minutes just randomly and ridiculously ignorantly touching various parts of my back (I swear, if I had eyes on the back of my head, I could swear he must have been multitasking by touching my back for 20 minutes, while either texting or watching HULU on his mobile device!üò†)

Then he, neither systematically nor knowledgeably massage my muscles in the highly regarded Chinese tradition of acupressure. The so called masseur Just randomly touched here and there without rhyme or reason.

When finished, I made sure to address my dissatisfaction with the man who appeared to be the manager (owner) while in the presence of the bad masseur.

All this manager did was, Smile and nod his head in agreement, while saying idiocies (in in his make-believe, "fake news" broken English) such as: [input heavy Chinese accent here. Hey what!? Relax! I'm ethnic myself, too! I can say this, (freedom of speech) my personal testimonial, without being denounced or condemned! With all do respect to the wonderful Asian community, my ethnic group also gets stereotyped in a humorous light, too!]
"Oh, That So Good! You No Like it" "That too bad!" Why You No Tell him, He No Good?" (I'm  obviously exaggerating. I'm pretty upset!) I said: this is a quiet place, sir, and you do not allow loud talking in this massage Hall. without disturbing the other clients and patrons.

I asked him, point blank if he was going to give me a credit or a partial reimbursement for my terrible experience. The man Totally ignored me and made no attempt to remedy the situation.

I did return to give J & J to give them a second chance. The next time I returned I had a different masseur.  this guy looked like he just came out of the kitchen and was more interested in what was for dinner than paying attention to me.!
This guy was by far, worse than the first one. He kept making random but more exaggerated back and forth hand motions that even hurt my face my ears, my temples and my neck!

I stopped him in the middle of it all, before he could do more damage.
(No one wants a repeat bad session)

I said, "Stop, sir I want a better massage therapist who knows what they're doing. I do not want to continue with you any further with you." (He just walked off and yelled in Chinese  for somebody new

This was 15 minutes into my massage. Then out comes this other massage therapist  who did a good job at giving me a very soft, unnecessary baby acupressure. She lulled me to sleep, did an efficient job at rubbing my body, but again, did not do the correct textbook  acupressure.

All she was more concerned about was how much money I was going to tip her afterwards. The massage was $25, I gave her a $12 tip. That's 50% gratuity right on the nose!! She made faces at me  and mumbled something unpleasant  sounding in Chinese.
I asked her if the tip was okay. She cynically exclaimed "it okay"..  Smirked, and walked away.

Again, the owner cared not to address my dissatisfaction, but rather, focused on the improvement from the first massage therapist to the next one I was assigned.

Needless to say. I appreciate J & J  for being an established massage parlor in Pasadena. What I dislike is : J & J not remedying this poor service situation by providing me a credit towards a future session.

Not Happy! Still expecting a credit.<//review>< Rating>

< Text>
Honestly places like this I believe are hit n miss and in my opinion and experience this location was a miss unfortunately. Del taco has been a staple in my family for many years and my mom and I just happens to be by this location and stopped for lunch and we went through the drive through. It wasn't busy at all and I had read really bad reviews on this location on Yelp. We went anyways giving the benefit of the doubt but I was very skeptical. People have had credit card fraud and terrible card handling issues there and I wasn't going to be next so we paid cash. But the girl running the window was very rude and curt and there were things from our order which were wrong, but not bad enough to go back. The service was very slow as well. We personally will not be returning but that doesn't mean we didn't just catch them on a bad day. Hope this helps someone!< /Text>
